      <p><b>Eswatini</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">ESS</span>-wah-<span style="font-size:90%">TEE</span>-nee</i></a>; <a href="/wiki/Swazi_language" title="Swazi language">Swazi</a>: <i lang="ss">eSwatini</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Nguni" title="Help:IPA/Nguni">[ɛswáˈtʼiːni]</a></span>), officially the <b>Kingdom of Eswatini</b> (Swazi: <i lang="ss">Umbuso weSwatini</i>), sometimes written in English as <b>eSwatini</b>, and formerly and still commonly known in English as <b>Swaziland</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">SWAH</span>-zee-land</i></a>; officially renamed in 2018),<sup id="cite_ref-:2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KingdEswatini_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KingdEswatini-12">[12]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> to its northeast and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> to its north, west, and south. At no more than 200 kilometres (120&nbsp;mi) north to south and 130 kilometres (81&nbsp;mi) east to west, Eswatini is one of the smallest countries in Africa; despite this, its climate and <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topography</a> are diverse, ranging from a cool and mountainous <a href="/wiki/Highveld" title="Highveld">highveld</a> to a hot and dry <a href="/wiki/Veld#Lowveld" title="Veld">lowveld</a>. </p>
      <p>The population is composed primarily of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Swazi_people" title="Swazi people">Swazis</a>. The prevalent language is <a href="/wiki/Swazi_language" title="Swazi language">Swazi</a> (<i>siSwati</i> in native form). The Swazis established their kingdom in the mid-18th century under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Ngwane_III" title="Ngwane III">Ngwane III</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bonner82_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonner82-13">[13]</a></sup> The country and the Swazi take their names from <a href="/wiki/Mswati_II" title="Mswati II">Mswati II</a>, the 19th-century king under whose rule Swazi territory was expanded and unified; the present boundaries were drawn up in 1881 in the midst of the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kuper86_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kuper86-14">[14]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a>, the kingdom, under the name of Swaziland, was a <a href="/wiki/British_protectorate" title="British protectorate">British protectorate</a> from 1903 until it regained its independence on 6 September 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-Gillis99_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gillis99-15">[15]</a></sup> In April 2018, the official name was changed from <i>Kingdom of Swaziland</i> to <i>Kingdom of Eswatini</i>, mirroring the name commonly used in Swazi.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KingdEswatini_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KingdEswatini-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government is an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a>, ruled by King <a href="/wiki/Mswati_III" title="Mswati III">Mswati III</a> since 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Elections are held every five years to determine the House of Assembly and the Senate majority. The current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of Swaziland">constitution</a> was adopted in 2005. <i><a href="/wiki/Umhlanga_(ceremony)" title="Umhlanga (ceremony)">Umhlanga</a></i>, the reed dance held in August/September,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Incwala" title="Incwala">incwala</a></i>, the kingship dance held in December/January, are the nation's most important events.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eswatini is a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a> with a small economy. With a <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> per capita of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>4,145.97, it is classified as a country with a lower-middle income.<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-22">[22]</a></sup> As a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Customs_Union" title="Southern African Customs Union">Southern African Customs Union</a> (SACU) and the <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa</a> (COMESA), its main local trading partner is South Africa; in order to ensure economic stability, Eswatini's currency, the <a href="/wiki/Swazi_lilangeni" title="Swazi lilangeni">lilangeni</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Fixed_exchange-rate_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Fixed exchange-rate system">pegged</a> to the <a href="/wiki/South_African_rand" title="South African rand">South African rand</a>. Eswatini's major overseas trading partners are the United States<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The majority of the country's employment is provided by its agricultural and manufacturing sectors. Eswatini is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC), the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. </p>
      <p>The Swazi population faces major health issues: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> and (to a lesser extent) <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> are widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> It is estimated that 26% of the adult population is HIV-positive. As of 2018, Eswatini has the 12th-lowest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy in the world</a>, at 58 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist-27">[27]</a></sup> The population of Eswatini is young, with a <a href="/wiki/Median_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Median age">median age</a> of 20.5 years and people aged 14 years or younger constituting 37.5% of the country's total population.<sup id="cite_ref-Demo_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demo-28">[28]</a></sup> The present population growth rate is 1.2%. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Eswatini" title="History of Eswatini">History of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Artifacts indicating human activity dating back to the early <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a>, around 200,000 years ago, have been found in Eswatini. Prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Rock_art" title="Rock art">rock art</a> paintings dating from as far back as c. 27,000 years ago, to as recent as the 19th century, can be found in various places around the country.<sup id="cite_ref-South_African_History_Online_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_African_History_Online-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The earliest known inhabitants of the region were <a href="/wiki/Khoisan" title="Khoisan">Khoisan</a> <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a>. They were largely replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Nguni_people" title="Nguni people">Nguni</a> during the great <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu migrations</a>. These peoples originated from the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">Great Lakes regions</a> of eastern and central Africa. Evidence of agriculture and iron use dates from about the 4th century. People speaking languages ancestral to the current <a href="/wiki/Sotho_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Sotho languages">Sotho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nguni_languages" title="Nguni languages">Nguni languages</a> began settling no later than the 11th century.<sup id="cite_ref-BonnerPhilip_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BonnerPhilip-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Swazi_settlers_.2818th_and_19th_centuries.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Swazi_settlers_(18th_and_19th_centuries)">Swazi settlers (18th and 19th centuries)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Swazi settlers (18th and 19th centuries)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Swazi settlers, then known as <i>the Ngwane</i> (or <i>bakaNgwane</i>) before entering Eswatini, had been settled on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Pongola_River" title="Pongola River">Pongola River</a>. Before that, they were settled in the area of the <a href="/wiki/Tembe_River" title="Tembe River">Tembe River</a> near present-day <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>. Continuing conflict with the <a href="/wiki/Ndwandwe" title="Ndwandwe">Ndwandwe</a> people pushed them further north, with <a href="/wiki/Ngwane_III" title="Ngwane III">Ngwane III</a> establishing his capital at <a href="/wiki/Shiselweni_Region" title="Shiselweni Region">Shiselweni</a> at the foot of the Mhlosheni hills.<sup id="cite_ref-BonnerPhilip_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BonnerPhilip-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under <a href="/wiki/Sobhuza_I" title="Sobhuza I">Sobhuza I</a>, the Ngwane people eventually established their capital at <a href="/wiki/Zombodze" title="Zombodze">Zombodze</a> in the heartland of present-day Eswatini. In this process, they conquered and incorporated the long-established clans of the country known to the Swazi as <i>Emakhandzambili</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BonnerPhilip_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BonnerPhilip-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A9cipient_Swazi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/R%C3%A9cipient_Swazi.jpg/220px-R%C3%A9cipient_Swazi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/R%C3%A9cipient_Swazi.jpg/330px-R%C3%A9cipient_Swazi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/R%C3%A9cipient_Swazi.jpg/440px-R%C3%A9cipient_Swazi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A9cipient_Swazi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A 19th-century Swazi container, carved in wood
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Eswatini derives its name from a later king named <a href="/wiki/Mswati_II" title="Mswati II">Mswati II</a>. <i>KaNgwane</i>, named for Ngwane III, is an alternative name for Eswatini, the surname of whose <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">royal house</a> remains <i>Nkhosi <a href="/wiki/House_of_Dlamini" title="House of Dlamini">Dlamini</a></i>. <i>Nkhosi</i> literally means "king". Mswati II was the greatest of the fighting kings of Eswatini, and he greatly extended the area of the country to twice its current size. The <i>Emakhandzambili</i> clans were initially incorporated into the kingdom with wide <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a>, often including grants of special <a href="/wiki/Ritual" title="Ritual">ritual</a> and political status. The extent of their autonomy, however, was drastically curtailed by Mswati, who attacked and subdued some of them in the 1850s.<sup id="cite_ref-BonnerPhilip_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BonnerPhilip-30">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With his power, Mswati greatly reduced the influence of the <i>Emakhandzambili</i> while incorporating more people into his kingdom either through conquest or by giving them refuge. These later arrivals became known to the Swazis as <i>Emafikamuva</i>. The clans who accompanied the Dlamini kings were known as the <i>Bemdzabuko</i> or <i>true Swazi</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Johnston,_W._and_A.K._-_South_African_Republic._Orange_Free_State,_Natal,_Basuto_Land,_Etc..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Johnston%2C_W._and_A.K._-_South_African_Republic._Orange_Free_State%2C_Natal%2C_Basuto_Land%2C_Etc..jpg/220px-Johnston%2C_W._and_A.K._-_South_African_Republic._Orange_Free_State%2C_Natal%2C_Basuto_Land%2C_Etc..jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Johnston%2C_W._and_A.K._-_South_African_Republic._Orange_Free_State%2C_Natal%2C_Basuto_Land%2C_Etc..jpg/330px-Johnston%2C_W._and_A.K._-_South_African_Republic._Orange_Free_State%2C_Natal%2C_Basuto_Land%2C_Etc..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Johnston%2C_W._and_A.K._-_South_African_Republic._Orange_Free_State%2C_Natal%2C_Basuto_Land%2C_Etc..jpg/440px-Johnston%2C_W._and_A.K._-_South_African_Republic._Orange_Free_State%2C_Natal%2C_Basuto_Land%2C_Etc..jpg 2x" data-file-width="3152" data-file-height="4269"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Johnston,_W._and_A.K._-_South_African_Republic._Orange_Free_State,_Natal,_Basuto_Land,_Etc..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>In this map of Southern Africa from 1896, Eswatini is labelled as "SWAZILAND"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The autonomy of the Swazi nation was influenced by British and Dutch rule of southern Africa in the 19th and early 20th centuries. In 1881, the British government signed a convention recognising Swazi independence despite the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a> that was taking place at the time. This independence was also recognised in the <a href="/wiki/London_Convention_(1884)" title="London Convention (1884)">London Convention of 1884</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Because of controversial land/mineral rights and other concessions, Swaziland had a <a href="/wiki/Triumvirate" title="Triumvirate">triumviral</a> administration in 1890 following the death of King <a href="/wiki/Mbandzeni" title="Mbandzeni">Mbandzeni</a> in 1889. This government represented the British, the Dutch republics, and the Swazi people. In 1894, a convention placed Swaziland under the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">South African Republic</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a>. This continued under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Ngwane_V" title="Ngwane V">Ngwane V</a> until the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a> in October 1899.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>King Ngwane V died in December 1899, during <a href="/wiki/Incwala" title="Incwala">incwala</a>, after the outbreak of the Second Boer War. His successor, <a href="/wiki/Sobhuza_II" title="Sobhuza II">Sobhuza II</a>, was four months old. Swaziland was indirectly involved in the war with various skirmishes between the British and the Boers occurring in the country until 1902.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="British_rule_over_Swaziland_.281906.E2.80.931968.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_rule_over_Swaziland_(1906–1968)">British rule over Swaziland (1906–1968)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: British rule over Swaziland (1906–1968)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 1903, after the British victory in the Second Boer War, Swaziland became a <a href="/wiki/British_protectorate" title="British protectorate">British protectorate</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Eswatini#Swaziland_Protectorate_(1906–1968)" title="History of Eswatini">Swaziland Protectorate</a>. Much of its early administration (for example, postal services) was carried out from South Africa until 1906 when the <a href="/wiki/Transvaal_Colony" title="Transvaal Colony">Transvaal Colony</a> was granted self-government. Following this, Swaziland was partitioned into European and non-European (or native reserves) areas with the former being two-thirds of the total land. Sobhuza's official coronation was in December 1921 after the regency of <a href="/wiki/Labotsibeni_Mdluli" title="Labotsibeni Mdluli">Labotsibeni</a>, after which he led an unsuccessful deputation to the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Privy Council of the United Kingdom">Privy Council of the United Kingdom</a> in London in 1922 regarding the issue of the land.<sup id="cite_ref-Vail91_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vail91-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the period between 1923 and 1963, Sobhuza II established the Swazi Commercial Amadoda which was to grant licences to small businesses on the Swazi reserves and also established the Swazi National School to counter the dominance of the missions in education. His stature grew with time and the Swazi royal leadership was successful in resisting the weakening power of the British administration and the incorporation of Swaziland into the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vail91_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vail91-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The constitution for independent Swaziland was promulgated by Britain in November 1963 under the terms of which legislative and executive councils were established. This development was opposed by the Swazi National Council (<i>Liqoqo</i>). Despite such opposition, elections took place and the first <i>Legislative Council of Swaziland</i> was constituted on 9 September 1964. Changes to the original constitution proposed by the Legislative Council were accepted by Britain and a new constitution providing for a House of Assembly and Senate was drawn up. Elections under this constitution were held in 1967.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.281968.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1968–present)">Independence (1968–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Independence (1968–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Following the 1967 elections, Swaziland was a protected state until independence was regained in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the elections of 1973, the constitution of Swaziland was suspended by King Sobhuza II who thereafter ruled the country by <a href="/wiki/Decree" title="Decree">decree</a> until his death in 1982. At this point, Sobhuza II had ruled Swaziland for almost 83 years, making him the <a href="/wiki/List_of_longest-reigning_monarchs" title="List of longest-reigning monarchs">longest-reigning monarch in history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-34">[34]</a></sup> A regency followed his death, with Queen Regent <a href="/wiki/Dzeliwe_Shongwe" class="mw-redirect" title="Dzeliwe Shongwe">Dzeliwe Shongwe</a> as head of state until 1984 when she was removed by the Liqoqo and replaced by Queen Mother <a href="/wiki/Ntfombi_Tfwala" class="mw-redirect" title="Ntfombi Tfwala">Ntfombi Tfwala</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mswati_III" title="Mswati III">Mswati III</a>, the son of Ntfombi, was crowned king on 25 April 1986 as King and <i><a href="/wiki/Ngwenyama" title="Ngwenyama">Ingwenyama</a></i> of Swaziland.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 1990s saw a rise in student and labour protests pressuring the king to introduce reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Thus, progress toward constitutional reforms began, culminating with the introduction of the current Swazi constitution in 2005. This happened despite objections by political activists. The current constitution does not clearly deal with the status of political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first election under the new constitution took place in 2008. Members of parliament were elected from 55 constituencies (also known as <i>tinkhundla</i>). These MPs served five-year terms which ended in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, Swaziland suffered an economic crisis, due to reduced SACU receipts. This caused the government to request a loan from neighbouring South Africa. However, they did not agree with the conditions of the loan, which included political reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During this period, there was increased pressure on the Swazi government to carry out more reforms. Public protests by civic organisations and <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a> became more common. Starting in 2012, improvements in SACU receipts have eased the fiscal pressure on the Swazi government. A new parliament, the second since promulgation of the constitution, was elected on 20 September 2013. At this time the king reappointed <a href="/wiki/Barnabas_Sibusiso_Dlamini" title="Barnabas Sibusiso Dlamini">Sibusiso Dlamini</a> as prime minister for the third time.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 19 April 2018, King <a href="/wiki/Mswati_III" title="Mswati III">Mswati III</a> announced that the Kingdom of Swaziland had renamed itself the Kingdom of Eswatini, reflecting the extant Swazi name for the state <i>eSwatini</i>, to mark the 50th anniversary of Swazi independence. The new name, Eswatini, means "land of the Swazis" in the Swazi language and was partially intended to prevent confusion with the similarly named <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KingdEswatini_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KingdEswatini-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Eswatini workers began anti-government protests against low salaries on 19 September 2018. They went on a three-day strike organised by the <a href="/wiki/Trade_Union_Congress_of_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade Union Congress of Swaziland">Trade Union Congress of Swaziland</a> (TUCOSWA) that resulted in widespread disruption.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Eswatini" title="Politics of Eswatini">Politics of Eswatini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Eswatini" title="Human rights in Eswatini">Human rights in Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mswati_III_King_of_Eswatini.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Mswati_III_King_of_Eswatini.jpg/220px-Mswati_III_King_of_Eswatini.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="329" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Mswati_III_King_of_Eswatini.jpg/330px-Mswati_III_King_of_Eswatini.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Mswati_III_King_of_Eswatini.jpg/440px-Mswati_III_King_of_Eswatini.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="1936"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mswati_III_King_of_Eswatini.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Ngwenyama" title="Ngwenyama">Ingwenyama</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Mswati_III" title="Mswati III">Mswati III</a> has been king of Eswatini since 1986.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monarchy">Monarchy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Monarchy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Eswatini is an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> with constitutional provision and Swazi law and customs.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> is the king or <i><a href="/wiki/Ngwenyama" title="Ngwenyama">Ngwenyama</a></i> (lit. <i>Lion</i>), currently <a href="/wiki/King_Mswati_III" class="mw-redirect" title="King Mswati III">King Mswati III</a>, who ascended to the throne in 1986 after the death of his father <a href="/wiki/King_Sobhuza_II" class="mw-redirect" title="King Sobhuza II">King Sobhuza II</a> in 1982 and a period of regency. According to the country's constitution, the <a href="/wiki/Ngwenyama" title="Ngwenyama">Ingwenyama</a> is a symbol of unity and the eternity of the Swazi nation.<sup id="cite_ref-Const05_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Const05-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By tradition, the king reigns along with his mother (or a ritual substitute), the <i><a href="/wiki/Ndlovukati" title="Ndlovukati">Ndlovukati</a></i> (lit. <i>She-Elephant</i>). The former was viewed as the administrative head of state and the latter as a spiritual and national head of state, with real power counterbalancing that of the king, but, during the long reign of Sobhuza II, the role of the <i>Ndlovukati</i> became more symbolic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The king appoints the prime minister from the legislature and also appoints a minority of legislators to both chambers of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of Swaziland">Libandla</a> (parliament) with help from an advisory council. The king is allowed by the constitution to appoint some members to parliament to represent special interests. These special interests are citizens who might have been electoral candidates who were not elected, or might not have stood as candidates. This is done to balance views in parliament. Special interests could be people of particular gender or race, people of disability, the business community, civic society, scholars, and chiefs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament">Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Swazi <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> Parliament, or <a href="/wiki/Libandla" class="mw-redirect" title="Libandla">Libandla</a>, consists of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Senate of Swaziland">Senate</a> (30 seats; 10 members appointed by the House of Assembly and 20 appointed by the monarch; to serve five-year terms) and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Assembly of Swaziland">House of Assembly</a> (65 seats; 10 members appointed by the monarch and 55 elected by <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">popular vote</a>; to serve five-year terms). The elections are held every five years after dissolution of parliament by the king. The last elections were held on 18 August and 21 September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The balloting is done in a <a href="/wiki/Nonpartisanism" title="Nonpartisanism">non-partisan</a> manner. All election procedures are overseen by the Elections and Boundaries Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>At Swaziland's independence on 6 September 1968, Swaziland adopted a <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster-style</a> constitution. On 12 April 1973, King Sobhuza II annulled it by decree, assuming supreme powers in all executive, judicial, and legislative matters.<sup id="cite_ref-Eisa08_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa08-46">[46]</a></sup> The first non-party elections for the House of Assembly were held in 1978, and they were conducted under the <a href="/wiki/Inkhundla" title="Inkhundla">tinkhundla</a> as electoral constituencies determined by the King, and established an Electoral Committee appointed by the King to supervise elections.<sup id="cite_ref-Eisa08_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa08-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until the 1993 election, the ballot was not secret, voters were not registered, and they did not elect representatives directly. Instead, voters elected an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_college" title="Electoral college">electoral college</a> by passing through a gate designated for the candidate of choice while officials counted them.<sup id="cite_ref-Eisa08_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa08-46">[46]</a></sup> Later on, a constitutional review commission was appointed by King Mswati III in July 1996, comprising chiefs, political activists, and unionists to consider public submissions and draft proposals for a new constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Drafts were released for comment in May 1999 and November 2000. These were strongly criticised by civil society organisations in Swaziland and human rights organisations elsewhere. A 15-member team was announced in December 2001 to draft a new constitution; several members of this team were reported to be close to the royal family.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2005, the constitution was put into effect. There is still much debate in the country about the constitutional reforms. From the early seventies, there was active resistance to the royal <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Eswatini" title="Elections in Eswatini">Elections in Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Nominations take place at the chiefdoms. On the day of nomination, the name of the nominee is raised by a show of hand and the nominee is given an opportunity to indicate whether he or she accepts the nomination. If he or she accepts it, he or she must be supported by at least ten members of that chiefdom. The nominations are for the position of Member of Parliament, Constituency Headman (<i>Indvuna</i>), and the Constituency Executive Committee (<i>Bucopho</i>). The minimum number of nominees is four and the maximum is ten.<sup id="cite_ref-EISA_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EISA-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Primary elections also take place at the chiefdom level. It is by <a href="/wiki/Secret_ballot" title="Secret ballot">secret ballot</a>. During the Primary Elections, the voters are given an opportunity to elect the member of the executive committee (Bucopho) for that particular chiefdom. Aspiring members of parliament and the constituency Headman are also elected from each chiefdom. The secondary and final elections takes place at the various constituencies called <a href="/wiki/Tinkhundla" class="mw-redirect" title="Tinkhundla">Tinkhundla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EISA_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EISA-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Candidates who won primary elections in the chiefdoms are considered nominees for the secondary elections at inkhundla or constituency level. The nominees with majority votes become the winners and they become members of parliament or constituency headman.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Eswatini" title="Foreign relations of Eswatini">Foreign relations of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eswatini is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The judicial system in Eswatini is a dual system. The 2006 constitution established a court system based on the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> model consisting of four regional Magistrates Courts, a High Court, and a Court of Appeal (the Supreme Court), which are independent of crown control. In addition, traditional courts (Swazi Courts or Customary Courts) deal with minor offenses and violations of traditional Swazi law and custom.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Judges are appointed by the King and are usually expatriates from South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The Supreme Court, which replaced the previous Court of Appeal, consists of the Chief Justice and at least four other Supreme Court judges. The High Court consists of the Chief Justice and at least four High Court judges.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chief_Justices">Chief Justices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Chief Justices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <ul>
       <li>1967–1970: Sir Isadore Victor Elgan</li> 
       <li>1998–2002: Stanley Sapire</li> 
       <li>2002–2007: Jacobus Annandale (acting)</li> 
       <li>2007–2010: <a href="/wiki/Richard_Banda" title="Richard Banda">Richard Banda</a><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>2010–2015: <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ramodibedi" title="Michael Ramodibedi">Michael Ramodibedi</a><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>2015–present: <a href="/wiki/Bheki_Maphalala" title="Bheki Maphalala">Bheki Maphalala</a><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Eswatini" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Eswatini">Military of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rangers_in_Action_22-African_Land_Forces_Summit-US_Army_Africa-13_MAY_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Rangers_in_Action_22-African_Land_Forces_Summit-US_Army_Africa-13_MAY_2010.jpg/220px-Rangers_in_Action_22-African_Land_Forces_Summit-US_Army_Africa-13_MAY_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Rangers_in_Action_22-African_Land_Forces_Summit-US_Army_Africa-13_MAY_2010.jpg/330px-Rangers_in_Action_22-African_Land_Forces_Summit-US_Army_Africa-13_MAY_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Rangers_in_Action_22-African_Land_Forces_Summit-US_Army_Africa-13_MAY_2010.jpg/440px-Rangers_in_Action_22-African_Land_Forces_Summit-US_Army_Africa-13_MAY_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2494" data-file-height="1669"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rangers_in_Action_22-African_Land_Forces_Summit-US_Army_Africa-13_MAY_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Swazi army officers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The military of Eswatini (<a href="/wiki/Umbutfo_Eswatini_Defence_Force" title="Umbutfo Eswatini Defence Force">Umbutfo Eswatini Defence Force</a>) is used primarily during domestic protests, with some border and customs duties. The military has never been involved in a foreign conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-crash_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crash-63">[63]</a></sup> The king is the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-Chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander-in-Chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> of the Defence Force and the substantive Minister of the Ministry of Defence.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are approximately 3,000 personnel in the defence force, with the army being the largest component.<sup id="cite_ref-sipri1_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sipri1-65">[65]</a></sup> There is a small air force, which is mainly used for transporting the king as well as cargo and personnel, surveying land with search and rescue functions, and mobilising in case of a national emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <div class="noresize" style="height: 246px; width: 200px; ">
        <map name="ImageMap_44e498b8fedd1ad9"><area href="/wiki/Hhohho_Region" shape="rect" coords="57,48,116,71" alt="Hhohho Region" title="Hhohho Region"><area href="/wiki/Lubombo_Region" shape="rect" coords="121,113,180,131" alt="Lubombo Region" title="Lubombo Region"><area href="/wiki/Manzini_Region" shape="rect" coords="40,121,96,141" alt="Manzini Region" title="Manzini Region"><area href="/wiki/Shiselweni_Region" shape="rect" coords="59,182,129,203" alt="Shiselweni Region" title="Shiselweni Region"></map>
        <img alt="A clickable map of Eswatini exhibiting its four districts." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Eswatini%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png/200px-Eswatini%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="246" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Eswatini%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png/300px-Eswatini%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Eswatini%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png/400px-Eswatini%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png 2x" data-file-width="732" data-file-height="899" usemap="#ImageMap_44e498b8fedd1ad9">
        <div style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Eswatini,_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored.png" title="About this image"><img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/resources/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;"></a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Eswatini" title="Regions of Eswatini">Regions of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eswatini is divided into four regions: <a href="/wiki/Hhohho_Region" title="Hhohho Region">Hhohho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lubombo_Region" title="Lubombo Region">Lubombo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manzini_Region" title="Manzini Region">Manzini</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shiselweni_Region" title="Shiselweni Region">Shiselweni</a>. In each of the four regions, there are several <i><a href="/wiki/Tinkhundla" class="mw-redirect" title="Tinkhundla">tinkhundla</a></i> (singular <i>inkhundla</i>). The regions are managed by a regional administrator, who is aided by elected members in each inkhundla.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The local government is divided into differently structured rural and urban councils depending on the level of development in the area. Although there are different political structures to the local authorities, effectively the urban councils are municipalities and the rural councils are the tinkhundla. There are twelve municipalities and 55 tinkhundla.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There are three tiers of government in the urban areas and these are city councils, town councils and town boards. This variation considers the size of the town or city. Equally, there are three tiers in the rural areas which are the regional administration at the regional level, tinkhundla and chiefdoms. Decisions are made by full council based on recommendations made by the various sub-committees. The town clerk is the chief advisor in each local council council or town board.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There are twelve declared urban areas, comprising two city councils, three town councils and seven town boards. The main cities and towns in Eswatini are <a href="/wiki/Manzini,_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Manzini, Swaziland">Manzini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbabane" title="Mbabane">Mbabane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nhlangano" title="Nhlangano">Nhlangano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siteki" title="Siteki">Siteki</a> which are also regional capitals. The first two have city councils and the latter two have town councils. Other small towns or urban area with substantial population are <a href="/wiki/Ezulwini" class="mw-redirect" title="Ezulwini">Ezulwini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matsapha" title="Matsapha">Matsapha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hlatikhulu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hlatikhulu">Hlatikhulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pigg%27s_Peak" class="mw-redirect" title="Pigg's Peak">Pigg's Peak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simunye" title="Simunye">Simunye</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Big_Bend,_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Bend, Swaziland">Big Bend</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>As noted above, there are 55 tinkhundla in Eswatini and each elects one representative to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Eswatini" title="House of Assembly of Eswatini">House of Assembly of Eswatini</a>. Each inkhundla has a development committee (<i>bucopho</i>) elected from the various constituency chiefdoms in its area for a five-year term. Bucopho bring to the inkhundla all matters of interest and concern to their various chiefdoms, and take back to the chiefdoms the decisions of the inkhundla. The chairman of the bucopho is elected at the inkhundla and is called <i>indvuna ye nkhundla</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
