      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Eswatini" title="Geography of Eswatini">Geography of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eswatini_Topography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Eswatini_Topography.png/330px-Eswatini_Topography.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Eswatini_Topography.png/495px-Eswatini_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Eswatini_Topography.png/660px-Eswatini_Topography.png 2x" data-file-width="1425" data-file-height="1411"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eswatini_Topography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topographic map of Eswatini
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Eswatini lies across a <a href="/wiki/Fault_(geology)" title="Fault (geology)">fault</a> which runs from the <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg" title="Drakensberg">Drakensberg</a> Mountains of <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, north through the Eastern highlands of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, and forms the <a href="/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley,_Kenya" title="Great Rift Valley, Kenya">Great Rift Valley</a> of Kenya.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>A small, landlocked kingdom, Eswatini is bordered in the North, West and South by the Republic of South Africa and by Mozambique in the East. Eswatini has a land area of 17,364&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (6,704&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). Eswatini has four separate geographical regions. These run from North to South and are determined by altitude. Eswatini is at approximately 26°30'S, 31°30'E.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Eswatini has a wide variety of landscapes, from the mountains along the Mozambican border to <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a> in the east and <a href="/wiki/Rain_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Rain forest">rain forest</a> in the northwest. Several rivers flow through the country, such as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Usutu_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Usutu River">Great Usutu River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Along the eastern border with Mozambique is the Lubombo, a mountain ridge, at an altitude of around 600 metres (2,000&nbsp;ft). The mountains are broken by the <a href="/wiki/Canyon" title="Canyon">canyons</a> of three rivers, the <a href="/wiki/Ngwavuma_River" title="Ngwavuma River">Ngwavuma</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maputo_River" title="Maputo River">Usutu</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mbuluzi_River" title="Mbuluzi River">Mbuluzi River</a>. This is cattle ranching country. The western border of Eswatini, with an average altitude of 1,200 metres (3,900&nbsp;ft), lies on the edge of an <a href="/wiki/Escarpment" title="Escarpment">escarpment</a>. Between the mountains rivers rush through deep gorges. Mbabane, the capital, is on the <a href="/wiki/Highveld" title="Highveld">Highveld</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eswatini_landscape.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Eswatini_landscape.jpg/330px-Eswatini_landscape.jpg" decoding="async" width="330" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Eswatini_landscape.jpg/495px-Eswatini_landscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Eswatini_landscape.jpg/660px-Eswatini_landscape.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2277" data-file-height="1062"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eswatini_landscape.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Landscape in Eswatini
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Veld" title="Veld">Middleveld</a>, lying at an average 700 metres (2,300&nbsp;ft) above sea level is the most densely populated region of Eswatini with a lower rainfall than the mountains. Manzini, the principal commercial and industrial city, is situated in the Middleveld.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Lowveld" class="mw-redirect" title="Lowveld">Lowveld</a> of Eswatini, at around 250 metres (820&nbsp;ft), is less populated than other areas and presents a typical African bush country of thorn trees and grasslands. Development of the region was inhibited, in early days, by the scourge of <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Eswatini contains three ecosystems: <a href="/wiki/Maputaland_coastal_forest_mosaic" title="Maputaland coastal forest mosaic">Maputaland coastal forest mosaic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambezian_and_mopane_woodlands" title="Zambezian and mopane woodlands">Zambezian and mopane woodlands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Drakensberg_montane_grasslands" class="mw-redirect" title="Drakensberg montane grasslands">Drakensberg montane grasslands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-71">[71]</a></sup> The country had had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.21/10, ranking it 142nd globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Eswatini" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Eswatini">Climate of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eswatini is divided into four climatic regions: the Highveld, Middleveld, Lowveld and Lubombo plateau. The seasons are the reverse of those in the Northern Hemisphere with December being mid-summer and June mid-winter. Generally speaking, rain falls mostly during the summer months, often in the form of thunderstorms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Winter is the dry season. Annual rainfall is highest on the Highveld in the west, between 1,000 and 2,000&nbsp;mm (39.4 and 78.7&nbsp;in) depending on the year. The further east, the less rain, with the Lowveld recording 500 to 900&nbsp;mm (19.7 to 35.4&nbsp;in) per annum.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Variations in temperature are also related to the altitude of the different regions. The Highveld temperature is temperate and seldom uncomfortably hot, while the Lowveld may record temperatures around 40&nbsp;°C (104&nbsp;°F) in summer.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The average temperatures at Mbabane, according to season: </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td>Spring</td> 
         <td>September–October</td> 
         <td>18&nbsp;°C (64.4&nbsp;°F) </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Summer</td> 
         <td>November–March</td> 
         <td>20&nbsp;°C (68&nbsp;°F) </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Autumn</td> 
         <td>April–May</td> 
         <td>17&nbsp;°C (62.6&nbsp;°F) </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Winter</td> 
         <td>June–August</td> 
         <td>13&nbsp;°C (55.4&nbsp;°F) </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Climate change in Eswatini is mainly evident in changing precipitation - including variability, persistent drought and heightened storm intensity. In turn, this leads to desertification, increased food insecurity and reduced river flows. Despite being responsible for a negligible portion of total global greenhouse gas emissions Eswatini is vulnerable to the impacts of climate change. The government of Eswatini has expressed concern that climate change is exacerbating existing social challenges such as poverty, a high HIV prevalence and food insecurity and will drastically restrict the country's ability to develop, as per Vision 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-www4.unfccc.int_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www4.unfccc.int-73">[73]</a></sup> Economically, climate change has already adversely impacted Eswatini. For instance, the 2015-2016 drought decreased sugar and soft drink concentrate production export (Eswatini's largest economic export). Many of Eswatini's major exports are raw, agricultural products and are therefore vulnerable to a changing climate.<sup id="cite_ref-www4.unfccc.int_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www4.unfccc.int-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Eswatini" title="Wildlife of Eswatini">Wildlife of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Flora_of_Swaziland" title="Category:Flora of Swaziland">Category: Flora of Swaziland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%99%D7%94_%D7%A9%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%94_-_Grewia_villosa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%99%D7%94_%D7%A9%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%94_-_Grewia_villosa.jpg/220px-%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%99%D7%94_%D7%A9%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%94_-_Grewia_villosa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%99%D7%94_%D7%A9%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%94_-_Grewia_villosa.jpg/330px-%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%99%D7%94_%D7%A9%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%94_-_Grewia_villosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%99%D7%94_%D7%A9%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%94_-_Grewia_villosa.jpg/440px-%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%99%D7%94_%D7%A9%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%94_-_Grewia_villosa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3105"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D7%92%D7%A8%D7%95%D7%99%D7%94_%D7%A9%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%A8%D7%94_-_Grewia_villosa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i><a href="/wiki/Grewia_villosa" title="Grewia villosa">Grewia villosa</a></i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are known to be <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="List of birds of Swaziland">507 bird species</a> in Eswatini, including 11 globally threatened species and four introduced species, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="List of mammals of Swaziland">107 mammal species</a> native to Eswatini, including the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/South-central_black_rhinoceros" title="South-central black rhinoceros">South-central black rhinoceros</a> and seven other endangered or vulnerable species.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Eswatini" title="Protected areas of Eswatini">Protected areas of Eswatini</a> include seven nature reserves, four frontier conservation areas and three wildlife or game reserves. <a href="/wiki/Hlane_Royal_National_Park" title="Hlane Royal National Park">Hlane Royal National Park</a>, the largest park in Eswatini, is rich in bird life, including <a href="/wiki/White-backed_vulture" title="White-backed vulture">white-backed vultures</a>, <a href="/wiki/White-headed_vulture" title="White-headed vulture">white-headed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lappet-faced_vulture" title="Lappet-faced vulture">lappet-faced</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_vulture" title="Cape vulture">Cape vultures</a>, raptors such as <a href="/wiki/Martial_eagle" title="Martial eagle">martial eagles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bateleur" title="Bateleur">bateleurs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Long-crested_eagle" title="Long-crested eagle">long-crested eagles</a>, and the southernmost nesting site of the <a href="/wiki/Marabou_stork" title="Marabou stork">marabou stork</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bgp_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgp-74">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Eswatini" title="Economy of Eswatini">Economy of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Swaziland_treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Swaziland_treemap.png/350px-Swaziland_treemap.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Swaziland_treemap.png/525px-Swaziland_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Swaziland_treemap.png/700px-Swaziland_treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="1107" data-file-height="865"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Swaziland_treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Swazi exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Eswatini's economy is diverse, with agriculture, <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a> and mining accounting for about 13% of GDP, manufacturing (textiles and sugar-related processing) representing 37% of GDP and services&nbsp;– with government services in the lead&nbsp;– constituting 50% of GDP. <a href="/wiki/Land_tenure" title="Land tenure">Title Deed</a> Lands (TDLs), where the bulk of high value crops are grown (sugar, forestry, and citrus) are characterised by high levels of investment and irrigation, and high productivity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>About 75% of the population is employed in <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a> upon <a href="/wiki/Swazi_Nation_Land" title="Swazi Nation Land">Swazi Nation Land</a> (SNL). In contrast with the commercial farms, Swazi Nation Land suffers from low productivity and investment. This dual nature of the Swazi economy, with high productivity in textile manufacturing and in the industrialised agricultural TDLs on the one hand, and declining productivity subsistence agriculture (on SNL) on the other, may well explain the country's overall low growth, high inequality and unemployment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Economic growth in Eswatini has lagged behind that of its neighbours. Real GDP growth since 2001 has averaged 2.8%, nearly 2 percentage points lower than growth in other <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Customs_Union" title="Southern African Customs Union">Southern African Customs Union</a> (SACU) member countries. Low agricultural productivity in the SNLs, repeated droughts, the devastating effect of HIV/AIDS and an overly large and inefficient government sector are likely contributing factors. Eswatini's public finances deteriorated in the late 1990s following sizeable surpluses a decade earlier. A combination of declining revenues and increased spending led to significant budget deficits.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Central_bank_swazi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Central_bank_swazi.jpg/290px-Central_bank_swazi.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Central_bank_swazi.jpg/435px-Central_bank_swazi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Central_bank_swazi.jpg/580px-Central_bank_swazi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Central_bank_swazi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Central Bank in Mbabane
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The considerable spending did not lead to more growth and did not benefit the poor. Much of the increased spending has gone to current expenditures related to wages, transfers, and subsidies. The wage bill today constitutes over 15% of GDP and 55% of total public spending; these are some of the highest levels on the African continent. The recent rapid growth in SACU revenues has, however, reversed the fiscal situation, and a sizeable surplus was recorded since 2006. <a href="/wiki/SACU" class="mw-redirect" title="SACU">SACU</a> revenues today account for over 60% of total government revenues. On the positive side, the external debt burden has declined markedly over the last 20 years, and domestic debt is almost negligible; external debt as a percent of GDP was less than 20% in 2006.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Eswatini's economy is very closely linked to the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_South_Africa" title="Economy of South Africa">economy of South Africa</a>, from which it receives over 90% of its imports and to which it sends about 70% of its exports. Eswatini's other key trading partners are the United States and the EU, from whom the country has received trade preferences for apparel exports (under the <a href="/wiki/African_Growth_and_Opportunity_Act" title="African Growth and Opportunity Act">African Growth and Opportunity Act</a>&nbsp;– AGOA&nbsp;– to the US) and for sugar (to the EU). Under these agreements, both apparel and sugar exports did well, with rapid growth and a strong inflow of foreign direct investment. Textile exports grew by over 200% between 2000 and 2005 and sugar exports increasing by more than 50% over the same period.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Southern_African_Customs_Union.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Southern_African_Customs_Union.svg/220px-Southern_African_Customs_Union.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Southern_African_Customs_Union.svg/330px-Southern_African_Customs_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Southern_African_Customs_Union.svg/440px-Southern_African_Customs_Union.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Southern_African_Customs_Union.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eswatini is part of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Customs_Union" title="Southern African Customs Union">Southern African Customs Union</a> (green).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The continued vibrancy of the export sector is threatened by the removal of trade preferences for textiles, the accession to similar preferences for East Asian countries, and the phasing out of preferential prices for sugar to the EU market. Eswatini will thus have to face the challenge of remaining competitive in a changing global environment. A crucial factor in addressing this challenge is the investment climate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The recently concluded Investment Climate Assessment provides some positive findings in this regard, namely that Eswatini firms are among the most productive in Sub-Saharan Africa, although they are less productive than firms in the most productive middle-income countries in other regions. They compare more favourably with firms from lower middle income countries, but are hampered by inadequate governance arrangements and infrastructure.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Eswatini's currency, the <a href="/wiki/Swazi_lilangeni" title="Swazi lilangeni">lilangeni</a>, is pegged to the <a href="/wiki/South_African_rand" title="South African rand">South African rand</a>, subsuming Eswatini's monetary policy to South Africa. Customs duties from the Southern African Customs Union, which may equal as much as 70% of government revenue this year, and worker <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> from South Africa substantially supplement domestically earned income. Eswatini is not poor enough to merit an <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a> programme; however, the country is struggling to reduce the size of the civil service and control costs at public enterprises. The government is trying to improve the atmosphere for <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Eswatini" title="Demographics of Eswatini">Demographics of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eswatini-demography.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Eswatini-demography.svg/350px-Eswatini-demography.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Eswatini-demography.svg/525px-Eswatini-demography.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Eswatini-demography.svg/700px-Eswatini-demography.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eswatini-demography.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Eswatini's population in thousands (1950–2021)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of Eswatini's population is ethnically <a href="/wiki/Swazi_people" title="Swazi people">Swazi</a>, mixed with a small number of <a href="/wiki/Zulus" class="mw-redirect" title="Zulus">Zulu</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Africans" class="mw-redirect" title="White Africans">White Africans</a>, mostly people of British and <a href="/wiki/Afrikaner" class="mw-redirect" title="Afrikaner">Afrikaner</a> descent. Traditionally Swazi have been <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_farmers" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsistence farmers">subsistence farmers</a> and herders, but most now mix such activities with work in the growing urban formal economy and in government. Some Swazi work in the mines in South Africa.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Eswatini also received <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> settlers and African refugees from <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>. Christianity in Eswatini is sometimes mixed with traditional beliefs and practices. Many traditionalists believe that most Swazi ascribe a special spiritual role to the monarch.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_centres">Population centres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Population centres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Eswatini" title="List of cities in Eswatini">List of cities in Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Eswatini" title="Languages of Eswatini">Languages of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/SiSwati_language" class="mw-redirect" title="SiSwati language">SiSwati</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> (also known as <i>Swati</i>, <i>Swazi</i> or <i>Siswati</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu language</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Nguni_languages" title="Nguni languages">Nguni</a> Group, spoken in Eswatini and South Africa. It has 2.5&nbsp;million speakers and is taught in schools. It is an official language of Eswatini, along with English,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> and one of the official languages of South Africa. English is the medium of communication in schools and in conducting business including the press.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>About 76,000&nbsp;people in the country speak <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tsonga_language" title="Tsonga language">Tsonga</a>, which is spoken by many people throughout the region is spoken by about 19,000&nbsp;people in Eswatini. <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> is also spoken by some residents of <a href="/wiki/Afrikaner" class="mw-redirect" title="Afrikaner">Afrikaner</a> descent. Portuguese has been introduced as a third language in the schools, due to the large community of Portuguese speakers from Mozambique<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> or <a href="/wiki/Northern_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Portugal">Northern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centro_Region,_Portugal" title="Centro Region, Portugal">Central Portugal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Eswatini" title="Religion in Eswatini">Religion in Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Eighty-three percent of the total population adheres to Christianity in Eswatini. <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_African_churches" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous African churches">indigenous African churches</a>, including <a href="/wiki/African_Zionist" class="mw-redirect" title="African Zionist">African Zionist</a>, constitute the majority of Christians (40%), followed by Roman Catholicism at 6% of the population. On 18 July 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ellinah_Wamukoya" title="Ellinah Wamukoya">Ellinah Wamukoya</a>, was elected <i>Anglican Bishop of Swaziland</i>, becoming the first woman to be a bishop in Africa. Fifteen percent of the population follows <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Traditional African religion">traditional religions</a>; other non-Christian religions practised in the country include <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (2%<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>), the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a> (0.5%), and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (0.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> There were 14 <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> families in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Kingdom of Eswatini does not recognise non-civil marriages such as Islamic-rite marriage contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Eswatini" title="Health in Eswatini">Health in Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Eswatini" title="HIV/AIDS in Eswatini">HIV/AIDS in Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2016, Eswatini has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_HIV/AIDS_adult_prevalence_rate" title="List of countries by HIV/AIDS adult prevalence rate">highest prevalence of HIV</a> among people aged 15 to 49 in the world (27.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-unaids16_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unaids16-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Eswatini" title="Education in Eswatini">Education in Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rural_primary_school_in_Eswatini.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Rural_primary_school_in_Eswatini.jpg/310px-Rural_primary_school_in_Eswatini.jpg" decoding="async" width="310" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Rural_primary_school_in_Eswatini.jpg/465px-Rural_primary_school_in_Eswatini.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Rural_primary_school_in_Eswatini.jpg/620px-Rural_primary_school_in_Eswatini.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Rural_primary_school_in_Eswatini.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A rural primary school in Eswatini
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education in Eswatini begins with pre-school education for infants, primary, secondary and high school education for general education and training (GET), and universities and colleges at the tertiary level. Pre-school education is usually for children 5-years or younger; after that, a student can enroll in a primary school anywhere in the country. In Eswatini, early childhood care and education (ECCE) centres take the form of preschools or neighbourhood care points (NCPs). In the country 21.6% of preschool age children have access to early childhood education.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Primary education in Eswatini begins at the age of six. It is a seven-year programme that culminates with an end-of-primary-school examination [SPC] in grade 7 which is a locally based assessment administered by the Examinations Council through schools. Primary Education is from grade 1 to grade 7.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The secondary and high school education system in Eswatini is a five-year programme divided into three years junior secondary and two years senior secondary. There is an external public examination (Junior Certificate) at the end of the junior secondary that learners must pass to progress to the senior secondary level. The Examinations Council of Swaziland (ECESWA) administers this examination. At the end of the senior secondary level, learners sit for a public examination, the Swaziland General Certificate of Secondary Education (SGCSE) and International General Certificate of Secondary Education (IGCSE) which is accredited by the Cambridge International Examination (CIE). A few schools offer the Advanced Studies (AS) programme in their curriculum.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are 830 public schools in Eswatini including primary, secondary and high schools.<sup id="cite_ref-SZEDSchoolList_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SZEDSchoolList-88">[88]</a></sup> There are also 34 recognised private schools with an additional 14 unrecognised. The biggest number of schools is in the Hhohho region.<sup id="cite_ref-SZEDSchoolList_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SZEDSchoolList-88">[88]</a></sup> Education in Eswatini as of 2009 is free at primary level, mainly first through the fourth grade and also free for orphaned and vulnerable children, but not compulsory.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1996, the net primary school enrollment rate was 90.8%, with gender parity at the primary level.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-89">[89]</a></sup> In 1998, 80.5% of children reached grade five.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-89">[89]</a></sup> Eswatini is home to a United World College. In 1963, Waterford School, later named <a href="/wiki/Waterford-KaMhlaba_United_World_College_of_Southern_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterford-KaMhlaba United World College of Southern Africa">Waterford Kamhlaba United World College of Southern Africa</a>, was founded as southern Africa's first multiracial school. In 1981, Waterford Kamhlaba joined the <a href="/wiki/United_World_Colleges" title="United World Colleges">United World Colleges</a> movement as the first United World College on the African continent, and the only African UWC until 2019 when UWC East Africa was established.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Adult and non-formal education centres are Sebenta National Institute for adult basic literacy and Emlalatini Development Centre, which provides alternative educational opportunities for school children and young adults who have not been able to complete their schooling.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Eswatini" title="University of Eswatini">University of Eswatini</a>, Southern African Nazarene University and Swaziland Christian University (SCU) are the institutions that offer university education in the country. A campus of <a href="/wiki/Limkokwing_University_of_Creative_Technology" title="Limkokwing University of Creative Technology">Limkokwing University of Creative Technology</a> can be found at Sidvwashini (Sidwashini), a suburb of the capital <a href="/wiki/Mbabane" title="Mbabane">Mbabane</a>. Ngwane Teacher's College and William Pitcher College are the country's teaching colleges. The Good Shepherd Hospital in <a href="/wiki/Siteki" title="Siteki">Siteki</a> is home to the College for Nursing Assistants.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Klopper12_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Klopper12-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The University of Eswatini is the national university, established in 1982 by act of Parliament, and is headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Kwaluseni" title="Kwaluseni">Kwaluseni</a> with additional campuses in Mbabane and <a href="/wiki/Luyengo" title="Luyengo">Luyengo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The Southern African Nazarene University (SANU) was established in 2010 as a merger of the Nazarene College of Nursing, College of Theology and the Nazarene Teachers College; it is in <a href="/wiki/Manzini,_Eswatini" title="Manzini, Eswatini">Manzini</a> next to the Raleigh Fitkin Memorial Hospital. It is the university that produce the most nurses in the country. As a university, it encampasses three faculties of which one is at Siteki which is the faculty of Theology and the other Two are found in Manzini which are the faculties of Education and the faculty of health Sciences <sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The SCU, focusing on medical education, was established in 2012 and is Eswatini's newest university.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> It is in Mbabane.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The campus of Limkokwing University was opened at Sidvwashini in Mbabane in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The main centre for technical training in Eswatini is the <a href="/wiki/Swaziland_College_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Swaziland College of Technology">Swaziland College of Technology</a> (SCOT) which is slated to become a full university.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> It aims to provide high quality training in technology and business studies in collaboration with the commercial, industrial and public sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Other technical and vocational institutions include the <a href="/wiki/Gwamile_Vocational_and_Commercial_Training_Institute" title="Gwamile Vocational and Commercial Training Institute">Gwamile Vocational and Commercial Training Institute</a> in <a href="/wiki/Matsapha" title="Matsapha">Matsapha</a>, the Manzini Industrial and Training Centre (MITC) in Manzini, Nhlangano Agricultural Skills Training Centre, and Siteki Industrial Training Centre. </p>
      <p>In addition to these institutions, the kingdom also has the Swaziland Institute of Management and Public Administration (SIMPA) and Institute of Development Management (IDM). SIMPA is a government-owned management and development institute and IDM is a regional organisation in <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, and Eswatini, providing training, consultancy, and research in management. North Carolina State University's <a href="/wiki/Poole_College_of_Management" title="Poole College of Management">Poole College of Management</a> is a sister school of SIMPA.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The Mananga Management Centre was established at <a href="/wiki/Ezulwini" class="mw-redirect" title="Ezulwini">Ezulwini</a> as Mananga Agricultural Management Centre in 1972 as an international management development centre offering training of middle and senior managers.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Eswatini" title="Culture of Eswatini">Culture of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Eswatini" title="Music of Eswatini">Music of Eswatini</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eswatini&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:King_Mswati_III,_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/King_Mswati_III%2C_2006.jpg/220px-King_Mswati_III%2C_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/King_Mswati_III%2C_2006.jpg/330px-King_Mswati_III%2C_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/King_Mswati_III%2C_2006.jpg/440px-King_Mswati_III%2C_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="959" data-file-height="1439"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:King_Mswati_III,_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>King <a href="/wiki/Mswati_III" title="Mswati III">Mswati III</a> at the reed dance festival where he will choose his next wife
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The principal Swazi social unit is the homestead, a traditional beehive hut thatched with dry grass. In a polygamous homestead, each wife has her own hut and yard surrounded by reed fences. There are three structures for sleeping, cooking, and storage (brewing beer). Larger homesteads also have structures used as bachelors' quarters and guest accommodation. </p>
      <p>Central to the traditional homestead is the cattle <a href="/wiki/Byre" class="mw-redirect" title="Byre">byre</a>, a circular area enclosed by large logs, interspersed with branches. The cattle byre has ritual as well as practical significance as a store of wealth and symbol of prestige. It contains sealed grain pits. Facing the cattle byre is the great hut which is occupied by the mother of the headman. </p>
      <p>The headman is central to all homestead affairs and he is often <a href="/wiki/Polygamous" class="mw-redirect" title="Polygamous">polygamous</a>. He leads through example and advises his wives on all social affairs of the home, as well as seeing to the well being of the family. He also spends time socialising with the young boys, who are often his sons or close relatives, advising them on the expectations of growing up and manhood. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sangoma" class="mw-redirect" title="Sangoma">Sangoma</a> is a traditional diviner chosen by the ancestors of that particular family. The training of the Sangoma is called "kwetfwasa". At the end of the training, a graduation ceremony takes place where all the local sangoma come together for feasting and dancing. The diviner is consulted for various purposes, such as determining the cause of sickness or even death. His diagnosis is based on "kubhula", a process of communication, through trance, with the natural superpowers. The <a href="/wiki/Inyanga" class="mw-redirect" title="Inyanga">Inyanga</a> (a medical and pharmaceutical specialist in western terms) possesses the bone throwing skill ("kushaya ematsambo") used to determine the cause of the sickness. </p>
      <p>The most important cultural event in Eswatini is the <a href="/wiki/Incwala" title="Incwala">Incwala</a> ceremony. It is held on the fourth day after the full moon nearest the longest day, 21 December. Incwala is often translated in English as "first fruits ceremony", but the King's tasting of the new harvest is only one aspect among many in this long pageant. Incwala is best translated as "Kingship Ceremony": when there is no king, there is no Incwala. It is <a href="/wiki/High_treason" class="mw-redirect" title="High treason">high treason</a> for any other person to hold an Incwala. </p>
      <p>Every Swazi may take part in the public parts of the Incwala. The climax of the event is the fourth day of the Big Incwala. The key figures are the King, Queen Mother, royal wives and children, the royal governors (<a href="/wiki/Induna" class="mw-redirect" title="Induna">indunas</a>), the chiefs, the regiments, and the "bemanti" or "water people". </p>
      <p>Eswatini's most well-known cultural event is the annual <a href="/wiki/Umhlanga_(ceremony)" title="Umhlanga (ceremony)">Umhlanga Reed Dance</a>. In the eight-day ceremony, girls cut reeds and present them to the queen mother and then dance. (There is no formal competition.) It is done in late August or early September. Only childless, unmarried girls can take part. The aims of the ceremony are to preserve girls' chastity, provide tribute labour for the Queen mother, and to encourage solidarity by working together. The royal family appoints a commoner maiden to be "induna" (captain) of the girls and she announces the dates of the annual ceremony over the radio. The chosen induna is expected to be an expert dancer and knowledgeable on royal protocol. One of the King's daughters acts as her counterpart during the ceremony. </p>
      <p>The Reed Dance today is not an ancient ceremony but a development of the old "<a href="/wiki/Umchwasho" title="Umchwasho">umchwasho</a>" custom. In "umchwasho", all young girls were placed in a female age-regiment. If any girl became pregnant outside of marriage, her family paid a fine of one cow to the local chief. After a number of years, when the girls had reached a marriageable age, they would perform labour service for the Queen Mother, ending with dancing and feasting. The country was under the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abstinence" title="Sexual abstinence">chastity</a> <a href="/wiki/Rite" title="Rite">rite</a> of "umchwasho" until 19 August 2005. </p>
      <p>Eswatini is also known for a strong presence in the handcrafts industry. The formalised handcraft businesses of Eswatini employ over 2,500 people, many of whom are women (per <i>TechnoServe Swaziland Handcrafts Impact Study</i>, February 2011). The products are unique and reflect the culture of Eswatini, ranging from housewares, to artistic decorations, to complex glass, stone or wood artwork. </p>
